22. Use and Maintenance of Improvements. Subdivider agrees that the use of any and all of 
the Required Improvements, for any person and by any person, shall be at the sole and exclusive risk 
of the Subdivider at all times prior to final acceptance by City. Subdivider agrees to assume all 
maintenance responsibilities for the Required Improvements until final acceptance by City. 
23. Title to Improvements. Title to and ownership of all Required Improvements shall vest in 
City for the Required Improvements. 
24. Final Inspection, Certification and Acceptance. All of the Required Improvements must 
be completed prior to the final inspection. Notice in writing, requesting final inspection, shall be 
submitted to the City Engineer at least five days prior to the anticipated date of final inspection. 
Upon the Subdivider’s satisfactory completion of the Required Improvements, the City Engineer shall 
certify that the Required Improvements have been satisfactorily completed, shall recommend 
acceptance of the Required Improvements by the City Council, and shall place the matter on the next 
available City Council agenda. 
25. Time of Essence. Time is of the essence in this Agreement. The Required Improvements 
shall be completed within two years of the date of this Agreement. The City Engineer may extend the 
time for completion of Required Improvements hereunder, upon good cause being shown by the 
Subdivider. Any extension must be documented in an amendment to this Agreement. Any such 
extension may be granted without notice to the Subdivider's surety and any extension so granted shall 
not relieve surety's liability on the bonds. 
26. Assignment of Contract. Neither this Agreement, nor any part of it, is assignable by 
Subdivider without the written consent of the City, not to be unreasonably withheld or delayed.  
27. Subdivider Not Agent of City. Neither Subdivider nor its agents or contractors are agents 
of City in connection with the performance of Subdivider's obligations under this Agreement. 
28. Notices. All notices required shall be in writing, and delivered in person or sent by 
registered mail, postage prepaid. A party or the surety may change the address by notice in writing to 
the other party and thereafter notices shall be addressed and transmitted to the new address.

ADDITIONAL OPTIONAL INFORMATION 
 
 
INSTRUCTIONS FOR COMPLETING THIS FORM 
Any acknowledgment completed in California must contain verbiage exactly    as appears 
above in the notary section or a separate acknowledgment form must be properly completed 
and attached to that document.  The only exception is if a document is to be recorded outside 
of California.  In such instances, any alternative acknowledgment verbiage as may be printed 
on such a document so long as the verbiage does not require the notary to do something that 
is illegal for a notary in California (i.e., certifying the authorized capacity of the signer).  Please 
check the document carefully for proper notarial wording and attach this form if required.  
● State and County information must be the State and County where the document signer(s) 
personally appeared before the notary public for acknowledgment.   
● Date of notarization must be the date that the signer(s) personally appeared which must 
also be the same date the acknowledgment is completed. 
● The notary public must print his or her name as it appears within his or her commission 
followed by a comma and then your title (notary public). 
● Print the name(s) of document signer(s) who personally appear at the time of notarization. 
● Indicate the correct singular or plural forms by crossing off incorrect forms (i.e., 
he/she/they, is/are) or circling the correct forms.  Failure to correctly indicate this 
information may lead to rejection of document recording. 
● The notary seal impression must be clear and photographically reproducible.  Impression 
must not cover text or lines.  If seal impression smudges, re-seal if a sufficient area permits, 
otherwise complete a different acknowledgment form. 
● Signature of the notary public must match the signature on file with the office of the county 
clerk.  
♣ Additional information is not required but could help to ensure this acknowledgment is not 
misused or attached to a different document.

♣ Indicate the capacity claimed by the signer.  If the claimed capacity is a corporate officer, 
indicate the title (i.e., CEO, CFO, Secretary).

MINIMUM SCOPE AND LIMIT OF INSURANCE  
Coverage shall be at least as broad as: 
Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office Form CG 00 01 covering CGL on an “occurrence” 
basis, including products and completed operations, property damage, bodily injury and personal & 
advertising injury with limits no less than $2,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate limit applies, 
either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location (ISO CG 25 03 or 25 04) or the 
general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.   
Automobile Liability:  Insurance Services Office Form Number CA 0001 covering any auto (Code 1), or if Contractor 
has no owned autos, hired (Code 8) and non-owned (Code 9) autos, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per 
accident for bodily injury and property damage. 
Workers’ Compensation insurance as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and Employer’s 
Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury or disease.  
Contractors Pollution Liability and/or Asbestos Pollution Liability and/or Errors & Omissions applicable to the 
work being performed, with a limit no less than $2,000,000 per claim or occurrence and $2,000,000 aggregate 
per policy period of one year. 
If the Subdivider maintains broader coverage and/or higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City 
requires and shall be entitled to the broader coverage and/or higher limits maintained by the Subdivider. Any 
available insurance proceeds in excess of the specified minimum limits of insurance and coverage shall be available 
to the City.

Other Insurance Provisions 
A. The General Liability, Automobile Liability, Contractors Pollution Liability, and/or Asbestos Pollution policies 
are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions: 
1. The City, its officers, officials, employees, and volunteers are to be covered as additional insureds with 
respect to liability arising out of work or operations performed by or on behalf of the Subdivider including 
materials, parts or equipment furnished in connection with such work or operations. General liability 
coverage can be provided in the form of an endorsement to the Subdivider’s insurance (at least as broad 
as ISO Form CG 20 10, CG 11 85 or both CG 20 10, CG 20 26, CG 20 33, or CG 20 38; and CG 20 37 forms if 
later revisions used). 
2. For any claims related to this project, the Subdivider’s insurance coverage shall be primary insurance 
coverage at least as broad as ISO CG 20 01 04 13 as respects the City, its officers, officials, employees, 
agents, and volunteers. Any insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its officers, officials, 
employees, agents, or volunteers shall be excess of the Subdivider’s insurance and shall not contribute 
with it. 
3. Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except with notice 
to the Entity. 
B. The Automobile Liability policy shall be endorsed to include Transportation Pollution Liability insurance, 
covering materials to be transported by Subdivider pursuant to the contract. This coverage may also be 
provided on the Contractors Pollution Liability policy. 
C. If General Liability, Contractors Pollution Liability and/or Asbestos Pollution Liability and/or Errors & Omissions 
coverages are written on a claims-made form: 
1. The retroactive date must be shown, and must be before the date of the contract or the beginning of 
contract work. 
2. Insurance must be maintained and evidence of insurance must be provided for at least five (5) years after 
completion of the contract of work. 
3. If coverage is canceled or non-renewed, and not replaced with another claims-made policy form with a 
retroactive date prior to the contract effective date, the Subdivider must purchase an extended period 
coverage for a minimum of five (5) years after completion of contract work. 
4. A copy of the claims reporting requirements must be submitted to the City for review. 
5. If the services involve lead-based paint or asbestos identification / remediation, the Contractors Pollution 
Liability shall not contain lead-based paint or asbestos exclusions. If the services involve mold identification 
/ remediation, the Contractors Pollution Liability shall not contain a mold exclusion and the definition of 
“Pollution” shall include microbial matter including mold.   
Acceptability of Insurers 
Insurance is to be placed with insurers authorized to conduct business in the state with a current A.M. 
Best rating of no less than A:VII if admitted in the State of California.

SUBJECT:
E 41st Place & Pacific Boulevard Trash Capture Project - Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with GSW Construction, Inc. for the E 41st Place and Pacific Boulevard Trash Capture project in the 
amount of $257,240; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $51,400; and authorize the Public Works Director to 
execute the agreement in substantially the form presented and issue change orders as allowed by the contract documents 
and within the contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
The E 41st Place and Pacific Boulevard Trash Capture project (Project) will install a trash capture device within an existing 
concrete channel located south of E 41st Place on Pacific Boulevard. The Project will support the City’s compliance with a 
San Francisco Bay Regional Water Quality Control Board’s (RWQCB) Municipal Regional Stormwater Permit (Permit). The 
Permit requires the City to reduce trash and litter discharge by 100 percent, relative to 2009 baseline values, by June 30, 
2025.
 
In 2023, the City awarded the professional design services for the Project to Schaaf & Wheeler Consulting Civil Engineers 
(Schaaf & Wheeler). Schaaf & Wheeler subsequently prepared a bid package for construction of a trash capture device. 
The engineer’s estimate which accompanied the bid package was $365,000.
 
The City advertised the project on January 23, 2025 and received and opened eight (8) bids on February 18, 2025. CEAU 
Co. DBA Castillon Company submitted the lowest bid to construct the project for a total price of $225,907; however, the 
bid package submitted by CEAU Co. DBA Castillon Company was determined to be not responsive. Subsequent review of 
the remaining bids showed that the next lowest bidder with a complete bid package was GSW Construction, Inc., with a 
total price of $257,240 to construct the project.  Staff has determined GSW Construction, Inc. Is the lowest responsive, 
responsible bidder and recommends that GSW Construction, Inc. be awarded the Agreement. The bids received are listed 
below in order of increasing bid amount.
 
Contractor
Grand Total Bid Amount
CEAU Co. DBA Castillon Company
$225,907.00
GSW Construction, Inc.
$257,240.00
W.R. Forde Associates, Inc.
$273,121.00
Selway Construction
$297,000.00
Golden Bay Construction, Inc.
$345,480.00
Central Pacific Construction
$347,970.40
Corcus Construction, Inc.
$362,300.00
91 of 316

--- page 92 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
CF Contracting, Inc.
$398,800.00
 
Staff believes there is moderate likelihood that unforeseen issues will arise during construction due to the requirement to 
divert water during construction and the limited work area. Accordingly, staff recommends a 20 percent contingency be 
established to address the moderate likelihood of unforeseen issues arising.
BUDGET IMPACT:
There are sufficient funds in the 41st Ave/Pacific Blvd Trash Capture project (#46C007) to fund this work in the amount of 
$257,240 and to establish a contingency reserve of $51,400.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation, repair, 
maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, facilities, 
mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or former use. (CEQA 
Guidelines Section 15301.)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

shall each submit one name from mediators listed by either the American Arbitration Association, 
the California State Board of Mediation and Conciliation, or other agreed-upon service. The 
mediator shall be selected by a blind draw.
The cost of mediation shall be borne equally by the parties. Neither party shall be deemed the 
prevailing party. No party shall be permitted to file a legal action without first meeting in mediation 
and making a good faith attempt to reach a mediated settlement. The mediation process, once 
commenced by a meeting with the mediator, shall last until agreement is reached by the parties but 
not more than 60 days, unless the maximum time is extended by the parties.

of the Contractor. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an endorsement to 
the Contractor’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, CG 11 85 or both CG 20 10, 
CG 20 26, CG 20 33, or CG 20 38; and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
2. For any claims related to this project, the Contractor’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance coverage at least as broad as ISO CG 20 01 04 13 as respects the Entity, its officers, 
officials, employees, and volunteers. Any insurance or self-insurance maintained by the Entity, 
its officers, officials, employees, or volunteers shall be excess of the Contractor’s insurance and 
shall not contribute with it. 
3. Each insurance policy required by this clause shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, 
except with notice to the Entity.
Builder’s Risk (Course of Construction) Insurance 
Contractor may submit evidence of Builder’s Risk insurance in the form of Course of Construction 
coverage. Such coverage shall name the Entity as a loss payee as their interest may appear.
If the project does not involve new or major reconstruction, at the option of the Entity, an Installation 
Floater may be acceptable. For such projects, a Property Installation Floater shall be obtained that 
provides for the improvement, remodel, modification, alteration, conversion or adjustment to existing 
buildings, structures, processes, machinery and equipment.  The Property Installation Floater shall 
provide property damage coverage for any building, structure, machinery or equipment damaged, 
impaired, broken, or destroyed during the performance of the Work, including during transit, 
installation, and testing at the Entity’s site.
Claims Made Policies – (If at all possible avoid and require occurrence type CGL policies)
If any coverage required is written on a claims-made coverage form: 
1. The retroactive date must be shown, and this date must be before the execution date of the 
contract or the beginning of contract work.
2. Insurance must be maintained and evidence of insurance must be provided for at least five (5) 
years after completion of contract work. 
3. If coverage is canceled or non-renewed, and not replaced with another claims-made policy form 
with a retroactive date prior to the contract effective, or start of work date, the Contractor must 
purchase extended reporting period coverage for a minimum of five (5) years after completion 
of contract work. 
4. A copy of the claims reporting requirements must be submitted to the Entity for review. 
5. If the services involve lead-based paint or asbestos identification/remediation, the Contractors 
Pollution Liability policy shall not contain lead-based paint or asbestos exclusions. If the services 
involve mold identification/remediation, the Contractors Pollution Liability policy shall not 
contain a mold exclusion, and the definition of Pollution shall include microbial matter, including 
mold. 
Acceptability of Insurers 
Insurance is to be placed with insurers authorized to conduct business in the state with a current A.M. 
Best rating of no less than A: VII, unless otherwise acceptable to the Entity.

Contractor hereby agrees to waive rights of subrogation which any insurer of Contractor may acquire

CITY OF SAN MATEO
RESOLUTION NO. ____ (2025)
APPROVING AN ALTERNATIVE PURCHASING PROCEDURE TO APPROVE A PURCHASE
CONTRACT FOR THE PURCHASE OF AN ABOVEGROUND FUEL TANK AND FUELING EQUIPMENT WITH 
PETROLEUM MARKETING EQUIPMENT IN THE TOTAL AMOUNT OF $125,606.39
WHEREAS, the State Water Resources Control Board requires that the two 10,000-gallon underground 
storage tanks (USTs) located at the City’s Corporation Yard be taken out of operation by December 31, 2025 to 
reduce the chances of soil contamination as a result of not having secondary containment; and
WHEREAS, the On-Site Fueling Station Replacement and Canopy Addition Project (Project) proposes to 
replace the USTs with an aboveground storage fuel tank (AST) and associated fueling appurtenances; and
WHEREAS, due to the urgency of this project and the anticipated several-month lead time of the AST 
and fueling equipment, City Council is being asked to approve the purchase of the tank and fueling equipment 
using an alternative purchasing procedure per Municipal Code Section 3.60.070(h)(3); and
WHEREAS, Municipal Code Section 3.60.070(h)(3) provides that the City may use any purchasing 
procedures approved by the City Council if the Council makes a finding concurrent with the award that the 
procedures are in the best interest of the City for that particular agreement.
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, RESOLVES that:
1.
This City Council action is categorically exempt from CEQA review as an “existing facility,” because it 
consists of the operation, repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of 
existing public or private structures, facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, 
involving negligible or no expansion of existing or former use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)
2.
In accordance with Municipal Code Section 3.60.070(h)(3), the purchase of an above ground fuel 
tank and fueling equipment from Petroleum Marketing Equipment $125,606.39 separate of the 
construction agreement and based on competitive quotes is in the City’s best interest due to:
a.
The state’s upcoming deadline of December 31, 2025 to take the existing USTs out of 
operation by December 31, 2025.
b.
The extensive procurement lead times for the aboveground fuel tank and fuel equipment.
c.
The potential hardship on the City in fueling gas-powered vehicles and equipment if the new 
aboveground fuel tank and fueling equipment is not in operation by December 31, 2025.
3.
The purchase contract of an aboveground fuel tank and fueling equipment with Petroleum 
Marketing Equipment in an amount of $125,606.39 is approved.  
4.
A contingency amount of $13,000 is approved. 
5.
The Public Works Director is authorized to execute the purchase contract in substantially the form 
presented on behalf of the City and issue change orders within the contingency amount.

This Public Works contract (“Contract”) is entered into by and between the City of San Mateo (“City”)

this Contract to Contractor for the amount set forth in Section 4, below.
2.
Contract Documents.  The Contract Documents incorporated into this Contract include and are
comprised of the Contract Book and all of the documents listed below. The definitions provided in
Article 1 of the General Conditions apply to all of the Contract Documents, including this Contract.

necessary and incidental for the timely performance and completion of the Work, including all
necessary labor, materials, supplies, tools, equipment, transportation, onsite facilities, and utilities,
unless otherwise specified in the Contract Documents. Contractor must use its best efforts to
diligently prosecute and complete the Work in a professional and expeditious manner and to meet or
exceed the performance standards required by the Contract Documents.

the Work in strict accordance with the terms and conditions of the Contract Documents, City will pay
Contractor $978,988 (“Contract Price”) for all of Contractor’s direct and indirect costs to perform the
Work, including all labor, materials, supplies, equipment, taxes, insurance, bonds and all overhead
costs, in accordance with the payment provisions in the General Conditions.

requirements for Final Completion, within 50 working days from the start date set forth in the Notice to
Proceed (“Contract Time”). By signing below, Contractor expressly waives any claim for delayed early
completion.

1.3(c) of the Supplementary General Conditions, if Contractor fails to complete the Work within the
Contract Time, City will assess liquidated damages in the amount of $3,500 per day, pursuant to
Section 8-1.10A of the 2018 Caltrans Standard Specifications, and such liquidated damages may be
deducted from City’s payments due or to become due to Contractor under this Contract.

SUBJECT:
On-Site Fueling Station Replacement and Canopy Addition – Purchase and Construction Contracts
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution approving an alternative purchasing procedure for a purchase contract with Petroleum Marketing 
Equipment for fueling equipment and a tank for the On-Site Fueling Station Replacement and Canopy Addition Project in 
the amount of $125,606.39, and establish a contingency reserve of $13,000 for the purchase contract; approve a 
construction contract with Armer Norman & Associates, Inc. in the amount of $978,988.00, and establish a contingency 
reserve in the amount of $150,000.00; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the purchase contract and 
construction contract in substantially the forms presented and issue change orders as allowed by the contract documents 
and within the contingency reserves.
BACKGROUND:
There are two 10,000-gallon underground storage tanks (USTs) located at the City’s Corporation Yard (1949 Pacific Blvd.) 
that store and distribute unleaded gasoline to 168 City vehicles and 10 pieces of equipment. The USTs are single-walled 
and were installed in 1967. The State Water Resources Control Board requires that these types of tanks be taken out of 
operation by December 31, 2025, to reduce the chances of soil contamination as a result of not having secondary 
containment. The On-Site Fueling Station Replacement and Canopy Addition Project (Project) proposes to install one 
10,000-gallon aboveground storage tank (AST) and associated fueling appurtenances, including dispensers, fuel 
management system, bollards, canopy, and monitoring systems, then to remove and dispose two existing 10,000-gallon 
USTs and associated fueling system and appurtenances. The cavity will be backfilled with clean fill and the surface will be 
restored.
 
In 2023, the City awarded the professional design services for the Project to Robertson Engineering, Inc. (Robertson). 
Robertson subsequently prepared a bid package for the Project. The engineer’s estimates were $150,000 and $825,000 for 
the tank/fueling equipment purchase and construction, respectively.
 
Purchase Contract with Petroleum Marketing Equipment
Originally, the procurement of the AST and fueling equipment was anticipated to be a part of the construction contract. 
Due to the urgency of this Project and the anticipated several-month lead times of the AST and fueling equipment, staff 
recommends purchasing the equipment separately. If the contractor procures the materials, it will add several months to 
the Project schedule potentially pushing the completion date past the state UST closure deadline of December 31, 2025. 
This would cause the City extreme hardship in fueling gas-powered vehicles and equipment as the existing USTs would be 
red-tagged and not allowed to be operated. 
 
Pursuant to San Mateo Municipal Code Section 3.60.070(h)(3), the City may use any purchasing procedure approved by 
the City Council if the City Council makes a finding concurrent with the award of the contract that the procedures are in 
117 of 316

--- page 118 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
the best interest of the City. Here, the solicitation of direct quotes, rather than a formal bid process, is in the best interest 
of the City because it significantly reduces the lead time needed prior to constructing the project and putting the new AST 
fueling station into service so that the City can meet the December 31, 2025 UST closure deadline. 
On January 28, 2025, the City solicited quotes to procure the AST and fueling equipment from three vendors: Northwest 
Pump, Shields Harper & Co., and Petroleum Marketing Equipment. Quotes were due on February 20, 2025, and a total of 
two (2) quotes were received. The quotes received are listed below in order of increasing amounts.

Based on the above, staff recommends for the City Council to adopt a Resolution approving an alternative purchasing 
procedure for a purchase contract with Petroleum Marketing Equipment in the amount of $125,606.39, and establish a 
contingency reserve of $13,000, and to approve a construction contract with Armer Norman & Associates, Inc. in the 
amount of $978,988.00, and establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $150,000.00.

agreements with Armer Norman & Associates, Inc. and Petroleum Marketing Equipment in the amounts of $978,988.00 
and $125,606.39, respectively, and to establish contingency reserves of $150,000 and $13,000, respectively, for a total of 
$1,267,594.39.

SUBJECT:
Citywide Small Trash Capture Project – Contingency Reserve Increase
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve a contingency reserve increase in the amount of $325,000 for the construction agreement with United Storm 
Water, Inc. for the Citywide Small Trash Capture Project, revising the original contingency reserve from $105,000 to 
$430,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to issue change orders within the contingency amount. 
BACKGROUND:
The San Francisco Bay Regional Water Quality Control Board (Regional Board) has mandated the City reduce trash 
discharged to the San Francisco Bay through the City’s storm drain system based on a 2009 baseline trash generation rate. 
The permit requires a 100 percent reduction in trash, relative to the 2009 baseline values, by June 30, 2025.
The Citywide Small Trash Capture Project (Project), currently under construction via a construction agreement with United 
Storm Water, Inc., will result in the City achieving approximately 90 percent reduction in trash discharge by installing 
around 370 small trash capture devices within the storm drainage system. The remaining 10 percent trash reduction will 
be achieved through a combination of a separate large capture device at 41st Ave/Pacific Blvd and approximately 85 
additional small trash capture devices. The construction contract for the large capture device is presented separately for 
Council consideration on this same April 7, 2025, meeting agenda.  
Due to the upcoming State deadline and the similarity in scope, it is in the City’s best interest to have United Storm Water, 
Inc. install the 85 additional small trash capture devices under the existing agreement to prevent delays. The existing 
contract was originally awarded to the lowest responsive, responsible bidder through a formal sealed bid process, and the 
scope of work is identical to the original contract. In addition, United Storm Water, Inc. has agreed to keep the same unit 
pricing for the additional devices. Failure to comply with trash reduction targets can result in enforcement actions or fines 
from the Regional Water Quality Control Board.  Based on these considerations, staff recommends for Council to authorize 
additional contingency funds for the Project.
To date, approximately $1,742 of the original $105,000 contingency reserve has been used to issue negotiated change 
orders. To mitigate risks associated with potential delays, streamline procurements, and to provide flexibility for staff to 
negotiate and execute contract change orders in a timely manner, staff recommends increasing the contingency reserve by 
$325,000, for a new total of $430,000 to address the anticipated change order(s) necessary to complete the project. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
Sufficient funds are available in the Citywide Small Trash Capture Project (46C001) project budget to fund this contingency 
increase.

Guidelines Section 15301.)

SUBJECT:
Marina Lagoon Vegetation and Water Quality Management — Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve a three-year agreement with Waterworks Industries, Inc. for Marina Lagoon Vegetation and Water Quality 
Management in the amount of $1,552,009, with two one-year options to extend, for a total potential amount not to 
exceed $2,662,963; approve a contingency reserve in the amount of $80,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to 
execute the agreement in substantially the form presented, to execute each optional one-year extension to the 
agreement, and sign change orders within the contingency reserve. 
BACKGROUND:
The City uses professional services to provide vegetation control and water quality management of the Marina Lagoon. 
The work includes control of nuisance plant growth, monitoring, and reporting and relies on the professional expertise of 
the consultant to formulate an effective control strategy compliant with water quality regulations. The aquatic nuisance 
growth season typically extends from April through September each year with winter storm clean-up requiring additional 
work. Waterworks Industries (Waterworks) has provided these services for the past 5 years. The agreement with 
Waterworks for the management of the Marina Lagoon expired February 5, 2025. 
A Request for Proposals (RFP) was issued on January 9, 2025. In addition to the published notice, the RFP was posted on 
the City website and provided to interested parties. The RFP required each consultant to provide a detailed plan for 
management of the lagoon including an integrated control strategy (i.e., chemical and mechanical control methods), 
personnel and machinery dedicated to the plan, monitoring and reporting tasks, and a cost for the proposed control plan. 
Staff received and reviewed proposals from 1) Solitude Lake Management and 2) Waterworks. Based on professional 
experience, proposal quality, demonstration of technical knowledge, and robustness of the proposed work plan, staff 
recommends awarding the agreement to Waterworks. Additionally, Waterworks’ proposal anticipated the regulatory 
requirement for a new aquatic pesticide permit in 2026, demonstrating a proactive understanding of lagoon vegetation 
management permitting.
BUDGET IMPACT:
Sufficient funding for Year 1 of this agreement is budgeted in the adopted Marina Lagoon program operating budget. The 
agreement includes a three-year term with two optional one-year extensions.  The first year of the agreement term is 
$500,828, with subsequent years of the agreement eligible for an annual CPI increase of 3 percent, beginning in Year 2. 
The annual cost breakdown is as follows:

Total: $2,662,963 
A contingency reserve in the amount of $80,000 is recommended to address any unforeseen costs. Sufficient funding for 
both Year 1 of the agreement and the $80,000 contingency is budgeted in the adopted Marina Lagoon program operating 
budget. Subsequent operating budgets will be proposed commensurate with future year costs.

public or private structures, facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no 
expansion of existing or former use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)

EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
Waterworks Industries, Inc. using subcontractor Blankinship, a Bowman Company, (“the 
Contractor”), will be responsible for water quality monitoring and regulatory compliance with the 
California State Water Resources Control Board (SWRCB) Aquatic Weed National Pollutant 
Discharge Elimination System Permit (“Permit”) and the California Department of Fish and 
Wildlife (CDFW) Streambed Alteration Agreement No. 1600-2013-0268-R3 for Routine 
Maintenance Activities (“Agreement”) for the City of San Mateo (“City”) as described below.  
Routine Inspection and Ambient Monitoring   
 
The Contractor will perform regular surveys and inspections of the lagoon at a minimum of once 
per week from April 1st – September 30th in which the entire lagoon will be surveyed for aquatic 
weed and algae growth using either aquatic plant mapping software and/or physical grab samples. 
The Contractor will perform more frequent inspections and monitoring contingent upon the 
duration and intensity of nuisance growth in the lagoon. Visual inspections of water quality and 
indicators of pollution (oil sheen, color, scum, etc.) will be performed during these inspections and 
will be recorded on weekly monitoring and service forms.  
During the scheduled weekly visits, the Contractor will inspect the entire lagoon for trash and 
debris in the water and along the banks. All trash will be removed using hand labor and approved 
equipment. If larger debris is present in the lagoon the Contractor will utilize their boat mounted 
crane or mobilize a multipurpose aquatic vessels for the removal. Material that is removed from 
the lagoon will be sorted and recycled into the appropriate recycling class at the designated staging 
and offloading area.
 
Mechanical Control Methods  
 
If the Contractor identifies that an area has reached the threshold sparse (0-25% cover), moderate 
(>25-50% cover), dense (>50-75% cover), or very dense (>75-100% cover), for needing 
mechanical aquatic weed control they will notify the City of San Mateo and advise which 
mechanical control method should be used such as harvesting including how many harvesters will 
be needed.  
 
If the City of San Mateo approves the recommended mechanical control with harvesters, the 
Contractor will provide skilled staff and state of the art equipment which features Tier 4 and 4i 
diesel engines to comply with current EPA and California emissions requirements as well as 
utilization of Bioflo, a Hydraulic fluid specifically classified as an environmentally acceptable 
lubricant (EAL) per the EPA’s 2013  US Vessel General Permit (VGP) for use in hydraulic 
systems for equipment that operates on water system.  
 
The Contractor will provide all other materials required to perform work safely and in a timely 
manner, pursuant to local, state and federal laws, and in accordance with the City’s Aquatic 
Pesticides Application Plan (APAP) and CDFW Agreement. If mechanical harvesting does occur 
on the lagoon it is understood that the aquatic vegetation as well as any floating material collected 
130 of 316

--- page 131 ---
Professional Services
Page 8 of 15
Rev 12/23
at public beaches, private dock areas, and along shorelines can be stockpiled in a location 
designated by the City of San Mateo so that it can dry out and then be hauled off for disposal.  If 
the City of San Mateo elects to haul off the wet and heavier material straight to the transfer station, 
the Contractor will provide the equipment to perform that option.  
 
As required by the CDFW Agreement and described below, pre-harvesting nesting bird surveys 
will occur if harvesting occurs during the nesting bird season. Survey results will be reported to 
CDFW prior to initiation of harvesting in case any active nest buffer areas are needed. The 
Contractor will keep daily records of any mechanical work performed on the lagoon to help the 
City document the types, quantities, and locations of the various mechanical control methods 
employed.  
CDFW Agreement Support 
 
The Contractor will provide a qualified biologist and/or biological monitor on an as-needed basis 
to conduct nesting bird surveys and establish protective buffer areas around active nests to 
minimize impacts of project activities to nesting birds found in and around Marina Lagoon. 
Nesting bird surveys will be conducted no more than 15 days prior to commencement of aquatic 
vegetation harvesting during the nesting bird season. Per the City’s CDFW Agreement, nesting 
bird season is defined as March 15 to August 30 for small bird species, and February 15 to 
September 15 for raptors.  
 
The Contractor will consult with CDFW and United States Fish and Wildlife Service, as 
appropriate, if active nests are encountered in areas that may be affected by project activities. 
Active nest buffers consistent with Section 2.22 of the Agreement will be established and nests 
will be monitored until project activities are complete or the young have fledged.  
 
Aquatic Herbicide And Algaecide Treatments  
 
Following routine lagoon inspections, the Contractor will notify the City of San Mateo of the need 
for a widgeon grass or algae treatment.  
 
Following approval and proper public notice, the Contractor will perform imazamox treatments in 
designated areas as soon as the widgeon grass reaches a threshold of eight (8”) to twelve (12”) 
inches off the lagoon bottom in the spring. It is anticipated that a second treatment in late May to 
June will be necessary to meet management objectives. For the rest of the season, the Contractor 
would determine if aquatic weeds and or algae are reaching threshold levels that would trigger 
harvesting or an additional aquatic herbicide application. If this threshold is met, the Contractor 
will notify the City of San Mateo of the need for a treatment. Following approval and proper 
public notice these treatments would be performed.  
 
Algae growth will be evaluated weekly. Reports of undesirable algae or vegetation from residents 
to the City will be investigated by the Contractor. If the density of algae is at or above a threshold 
impacting the beneficial uses of the lagoon, a treatment will be considered. Following approval 
and proper public notice, algae would be treated with products containing the active ingredients 
Sodium Carbonate Peroxyhydrate, Hydrogen Dioxide and/or Peroxyacetic Acid.  
131 of 316

--- page 132 ---
Professional Services
Page 9 of 15
Rev 12/23
 Regulatory Compliance  
 
The Contractor will use one application vessels based on the size and location of the treatment 
needed. The Contractor will fill out the designated forms to keep records of all treatments 
performed on the lagoon which will be used for record keeping and Permit compliance.    
 
Kickoff and Planning Meeting 
 
At least 15 days prior to the first use of aquatic herbicides in a calendar year, the City must notify 
potentially affected public agencies with a statement of the intent to apply algaecides and/or 
aquatic herbicides. Prior to the aquatic weed control season, the Contractor will assist the City 
with public notification requirements. This includes, but is not limited to, identifying potentially 
affected public agencies and providing guidance on which herbicides to identify in the notice, the 
purpose of their use, the time period and locations of expected use, and water use restrictions 
and/or precautions for the use of those materials.  
 
The Contractor will meet with representatives from the City to discuss the applications planned for 
the Permit year and what changes, if any, are made to how algae and/or aquatic vegetation will be 
managed. 
 
Sample Collection and Analysis 
 
Based on the City’s APAP and NOI and historic application data, the Contractor will collect and 
submit for analysis appropriate surface water samples collected before (Pre-Application), during 
(Application) and after the application (Post-Application) according to Permit requirements. Pre-
Application samples will be taken up to 24 hours before the start of treatment from within the 
treatment area. For full-lagoon applications, application samples will only be taken if water is 
leaving the system and will be collected from the receiving water near the point of discharge. For 
partial-lagoon applications, application samples will be taken directly outside of the treatment 
area. Post-application samples will be taken up to 7 days after the application has been deemed 
complete and will be collected from within the treatment area.  
 
To avoid cross-contamination, different intermediate sampling containers will be used for each 
sample collected and any equipment that makes contact with a water body during sampling will be 
cleaned using a phosphate-free detergent product (e.g. Liquinox). Should there be any copper 
treatments, copper samples taken for the purpose of analyzing dissolved copper would be field 
filtered using a 0.45 micron luer lock filter before being preserved in nitric acid. During or shortly 
after sample collection, the Contractor will perform necessary field chemistry analysis (pH, 
electrical conductivity (EC), dissolved oxygen (DO) and turbidity) and submit properly preserved 
and labeled samples under chain of custody procedures to a qualified analytical laboratory for 
chemical analysis.   
 
The Contractor will ensure that water quality monitoring instruments are regularly serviced, 
maintained, calibrated, and verified against calibration standards to measure all the Permit-
required parameters accurately and precisely. The Contractor will maintain a log of all calibration 
results and archive those records for a minimum of three years. The Contractor’s staff will be 
trained in the use and maintenance of these instruments and be able to identify measurement errors 
132 of 316

--- page 133 ---
Professional Services
Page 10 of 15
Rev 12/23
and troubleshoot equipment in the field. Evidence of training records will be provided to the City 
upon request. When in the field, the Contractor will carry spare parts and replacements as a 
redundancy to reduce the possibility of missing a field measurement.   
 
When conducting water tests the Contractor will use a variety of sampling equipment, including 
long-arm sampling poles, Van Dorn collectors, and peristaltic pumps that allow collection of 
samples from sites with difficult access. Additionally, the Contractor may need to deploy kayaks 
and/or a motorized boat to collect water samples from Marina Lagoon. The Contractor’s staff will 
be trained in clean sampling techniques and proper sampling handling to minimize the chance of 
inadvertent contamination. Evidence of training records will be provided to the City upon request.
The Contractor will recommend herbicide applications (number of applications and type of aquatic 
pesticide) to manage vegetation in the Marina Lagoon. Herbicide applications, including, but not 
limited to, types of chemicals used and sampling frequency, will be made in conformance with 
Permit requirements.

Project Equipment 
 
A minimum of one harvester will be dedicated to Marina Lagoon at all times for the duration of 
the nuisance growth season. This unit shall be on shore and ready to launch at all times for the 
duration of the plant growth season. 
The Contractor’s maximum response time for mobilization of harvesting, rotovation, transport, 
spray and shoreline support equipment will be 48 hours.  
 
If any equipment listed below goes out of working order, the Contractor will replace it within 
twenty-four (24) hours to ensure continual service, particularly during the high plant growth 
period.  
 
All equipment will have proper identification and licensing required by law and will be cleaned, 
drained and dried to ensure no invasive species are being introduced into the lagoon.  
  Beach Maintenance  
 
The Contractor will provide weekly cleaning and maintenance of the sand beaches of Lakeshore 
and Aquatic Parks and understands that the goal of this cleaning will be to reduce the presence of 
coliform bacteria by preventing the accumulation of algae and debris and other material that can 
harbor these pathogens. 
 
Cleanup Events 
 
The Contractor will provide all equipment, staff, and experience to mobilize and address post-
storm or non-routine cleanup events as requested to remove debris and litter. This will include 
inspecting and removing litter and debris collected at the trash boom downstream from Laurel 
Creek.

the Contractor by phone. The Contractor will respond back immediately to City of San Mateo staff 
by phone, as well as with an email confirmation of this dissatisfaction, noting the resolution 
programs to be implemented.

2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONSULTANT has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.

injury or disease.

profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate

shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONSULTANT.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONSULTANT; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONSULTANT including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONSULTANT’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the CONSULTANT’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONSULTANT’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.

SUBJECT:
Gateway Park Pedestrian Bridge Replacement Project – Bid Rejection
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to reject all bids received for the Gateway Park Pedestrian Bridge Replacement Project.
BACKGROUND:
The Gateway Park Pedestrian Bridge, located in the City’s Gateway Park was constructed in 1990 and is 35 years old. 
Gateway Park serves the downtown and North Central communities as it is located at the corner of 2nd Avenue and S. 
Grant Street. The pedestrian bridge consists of steel tube trusses, spanning over 75 feet over San Mateo Creek with 
concrete footings on either end. Preliminary inspections and evaluation of the steel superstructure of the bridge have 
indicated signs of deterioration and corrosion, further demonstrating that the bridge requires replacement. To address 
this, City staff developed the Gateway Park Pedestrian Bridge Replacement Project (Project) to replace the bridge structure 
and address Americans with Disabilities Act (ADA) compliance issues at the bridge approaches. 
Biggs Cardosa Associates, Inc. (BCA) was awarded an agreement in March 2024 to design the Project and completed design 
in January 2025. The design included an additive bid item to galvanize the bridge in addition to a three-layer paint system. 
The Engineer’s estimate for the base bid was $420,000 and $34,000 for the additive bid item for a total estimate of 
$454,000. 
In accordance with Municipal Code Section 3.60.030, a competitive public process was used to obtain bids for the Project. 
A notice inviting sealed proposals was issued to advertise the Project on January 9, 2025. On the February 6, 2025, bid 
opening date, six (6) bids were received. Per the requirements specified in the Contract Book, bids were compared based 
on the total bid amount, which includes the Base Bid plus Additive Bid Item A. 
Contractor
Base Bid Amount
Additive Bid Item A
Total Bid Amount
Globe Engineering Development
$428,100.00
$30,000.00
$458,100.00

$486,225.00

$34,000.00
$667,369.00
Prior to bidding the Project, BCA reached out to bridge manufacturers to determine the current lead time in procuring a 
prefabricated steel truss bridge of this size. At the time, the Project team determined a conservative lead time of 20 weeks 
and that there would be sufficient time to onboard a contractor, prepare and review submittals/shop drawings, and 
139 of 316

--- page 140 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
fabricate/deliver/install the bridge within the calendar year’s in-water work window of May 27 to October 31 stipulated by 
the Project’s Streambed Alteration Agreement with the California Department of Fish and Wildlife (CDFW). This work 
window is to minimize adverse impacts to sensitive species near San Mateo Creek. 
Upon receiving bids, staff reached out to the lowest bidder’s bridge manufacturer to confirm current fabrication lead 
times. Unfortunately, lead times have increased, and the bridge manufacturer indicated it would take approximately 23-31 
weeks for bridge delivery to the Project site. An additional four to six weeks of time would be required for City review of 
the submittals and shop drawings to verify what is being installed matches the approved plans, design criteria, and Project 
specifications. Therefore, the estimated bridge delivery is anticipated in December, which would result in the City being 
out of compliance with the required work window from its CDFW permit. 
Therefore, due to schedule constraints, staff recommends rejecting all bids pursuant to San Mateo Municipal Code section 
3.60.040(a)(4). City staff will readvertise the Project in Summer 2025 to allow for adequate time for bridge procurement, 
and the project will start construction in Summer 2026 to complete installation of the bridge within CDFW’s required work 
window.
BUDGET IMPACT:
While there is no direct budget impact for the rejection of bids, rebidding the project in the future may result in increased 
project costs, especially relative to concerns for federal action on tariffs, such as in regard to steel.  Staff anticipates this 
could increase direct costs for the bridge by approximately $50,000. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This action by the City Council to reject all bids for the Gateway Park Pedestrian Bridge Replacement Project is not a 
project subject to CEQA, because CEQA does not apply to projects which are rejected or disapproved. (CEQA Guidelines 
Section 15270).
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
RESOLUTION NO. ____ (2025)
REJECTING ALL BIDS FOR THEGATEWAY PARK PEDESTRIAN BRIDGE REPLACEMENT PROJECT
WHEREAS, work began on the design phase of the Gateway Park Pedestrian Bridge Replacement Project 
(Project) in March 2024, which includes replacement of the pedestrian bridge structure and addresses American 
with Disabilities Act compliance issues at the bridge approaches; and
WHEREAS, the City advertised the Project on January 9, 2025 in accordance with Section 3.60.040 of the 
Municipal Code; and
WHEREAS, on the February 6, 2025 bid opening date, six (6) bids were received; and
WHEREAS, the Project cannot move forward this calendar year due to current bridge procurement lead 
times and environmental in-water work window deadlines; and
WHEREAS, pursuant to San Mateo Municipal Code section 3.60.040(a)(4), the City Council, at its 
discretion, may reject all bids received; and
WHEREAS, staff recommends for the City Council to reject all bids which will allow the City to 
readvertise the Project in Summer 2025 to meet the procurement lead times and environmental in-water work 
window deadlines.
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY RESOLVES 
that:
1.
This council action is not a project subject to CEQA, because CEQA does not apply to projects which are 
rejected or disapproved. The proposed action is to reject all bids and readvertise the Project in Summer 
2025. If a lowest responsive, responsible bidder is determined in Summer 2025, then the Project will be 
subject to future Council consideration and CEQA review. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15270.)
2.
In accordance with the provisions of San Mateo Municipal Code Section 3.60.040(a)(4), all bids for the 
Gateway Park Pedestrian Bridge Replacement Project are rejected.

SUBJECT:
Enterprise Resource Planning Support Service - Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve a new Statement of Work to the master services agreement with Collaborative Solutions, LLC for Enterprise 
Resource Planning Support Service (ERP) post-production support services in the amount of $242,000 and authorize the 
City Manager to approve the Statement of Work in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
In February 2022, the City Council awarded a contract to Collaborative Solutions, LLC in the amount of $2,527,160 as part 
of the enterprise resource planning (ERP) system replacement project. Collaborative Solutions, LLC is now known as 
Cognizant.  Following the approval of the original agreement, the City Council has approved several change orders for 
implementation services as part of the Cognizant master services agreement. This was due to delays with the testing stage, 
staff and consultant turnover, time needed to address the complex human resources and payroll calculations needed for 
City and San Mateo Consolidated Fire employees, and the Project re-planning activities. The City Council approved the last 
implementation change order for Cognizant, Change Order No. 8, at the January 21, 2025, City Council meeting which 
brought the total contract with Cognizant to $4,739,292.
 
The Workday ERP supports the City’s core administrative functions of Human Capital Management (HCM), Payroll, and 
Core Financials. The ERP implementation has occurred in phases. Phase 1 covered Core Financials, began in March 2022, 
and went live on November 1, 2022. Phase 2 began in October 2022 and covers HCM and Payroll. The Plan, Architect, 
Configure, Test, and Deployment Stages of Phase 2 have now been completed, and the City and San Mateo Consolidated 
Fire went live on March 16, 2024. 
 
At this time, City staff recommends adding a new Statement of Work to the contract with Cognizant to provide post-
production support (Lean-On Support Services). With the deployment stage of Workday complete, the implementation 
support phase will come to an end on April 11, 2025. A new Statement of Work with Cognizant will allow the City to access 
the resources of the Cognizant consultants on an hourly basis to help troubleshoot and fix any post-production issues with 
HCM, Payroll and Core Financials. This allows City staff to have direct access to support from the same consultants that 
helped configure the system. The contract also allows for continued knowledge transfer on Workday functionality to City 
staff with the goal of reducing the City’s reliance on Cognizant’s support services. The master services agreement with 
Cognizant allows for this new Statement of Work which will cost $242,000 over two years and will bring the overall 
Cognizant contract to $4,981,292.
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no fiscal impact to adding this new Statement of Work. The Finance Department budgeted for the first year of 
Workday post-production support in their FY 24-25 operating budget. The cost for the second year of the contract will be 
142 of 316

--- page 143 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
included in the FY 25-26 operating budget for the Finance Department.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
The Collaborative Solutions new Statement of Work is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or 
administrative activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines 
Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

b.

Account Number: 72-4674

City Council
FROM:
Alex Khojikian, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Public Works Department
MEETING DATE:
April 07, 2025 
SUBJECT:
Temporary Standby Generator for Dale Avenue Pump Station Upgrade – Contract Change Order
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Contract Change Order No. 8 to the Agreement with Herc Rentals, Inc. for a temporary emergency standby 
generator to support the Dale Ave Pump Station Upgrade project in an amount not to exceed $66,944.28, increasing the 
total agreement amount to $781,731.99; increase the contingency reserve by $22,350; extend the Agreement term to 
April 30, 2025; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the change order in substantially the form presented 
and issue change orders within the contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
The Basins 2 & 3 Collection System Improvements (Basins 2 & 3) is a Clean Water Program project that increases capacity 
and improves flow management to prevent sanitary sewer overflows in several areas throughout the City, including one at 
Dale Avenue Pump Station (DAPS). The DAPS Upgrade project included refurbishment of force mains, pump station 
equipment upgrades, and replacement of the existing emergency standby generator. 
In October 2019, City Council awarded an agreement to Anvil Builders, Inc. (Anvil) to construct the DAPS Upgrade project. 
Anvil’s scope of work is nearly complete; however, there is still ongoing work associated with installation of a permanent 
emergency standby generator. The emergency standby generator at DAPS is critical, providing backup power for the 
pumps and facility during power failures. DAPS is the City’s largest sewer pump station, with a significant portion of overall 
wastewater flow routed through the station. Due to Bay Area Air Quality Management District requirements to comply 
with the latest air quality emission standards, installation of new pollution abatement equipment for the generator is 
required. While installing the new generator and pollution abatement equipment, a temporary standby generator is 
required to ensure continuous power capability at the station. 
In August 2022, City Council approved a $222,090.41 agreement with Herc Rentals, Inc. (Herc) to provide a temporary 
standby generator required to support the DAPS Upgrade Project throughout the remainder of Anvil’s efforts to install the 
permanent emergency standby generator. The Council also approved establishing a $110,046 contingency reserve in case 
of unforeseen conditions or delays. At the time of the agreement approval, the new permanent emergency generator was 
expected to be installed by the end of Summer 2023. 
In July 2023, the Public Works Director utilized the contingency reserve to execute Contract Change Order No. 1, adding 
$107,170.16 to the agreement. This change order addressed additional costs not accounted for in the original quote and 
agreement, such as utilizing longer cables to relocate the temporary generator from the public right of way onto the DAPS 
site. Residential property owners adjacent to the DAPS site raised a concern that storing the temporary generator in the 
public right of way impacted residential parking, so the temporary generator was relocated onto the DAPS property to 
address this concern. 
154 of 316

--- page 155 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
In August 2023, City Council approved Contract Change Order No. 2 to increase the total agreement value by $107,216.64, 
to extend contract end date to January 2024 and approved an additional contingency reserve of $80,000. In February 
2024, the Public Works Director utilized the contingency reserve to execute Contract Change Order No. 3 to extend the use 
of the temporary generator through April 2024 and increase the agreement value by $80,081.32. 
In April 2024, City Council approved Contract Change Order No. 4 to increase the total agreement value by $66,565.48 and 
approved an increase in the contingency reserve of $45,000. In August 2024, the Public Works Director utilized the 
contingency reserve to execute Contract Change Order No. 5 to extend the use of the temporary generator through 
September 2024 and increase the agreement value by $43,887.90. 
In September 2024, City Council approved Contract Change Order No. 6 to increase the total agreement value by 
$43,887.90 to extend the contract end date to November 2024 and approved a $45,000 increase to the contingency 
reserve. In December 2024, the Public Works Director utilized the continency reserve to execute Contract Change Order 
No. 7 to extend the use of the temporary generator through January 2025 and to increase the total agreement value by 
$43,887.90. 
There have been continued challenges in completing installation of the permanent generator at DAPS due to continued 
supply chain delays and completion of seismic design updates that have extended the anticipated completion date to the 
end of March 2025. The permanent generator and ancillary pollution abatement equipment delivery was delayed due to 
vendor and weather issues. The permanent generator assembly was delivered in early February. Staff were negotiating 
credits with Herc to cover the extended costs of the temporary generator while the permanent generator was being 
installed to potentially avoid another contract change order.  However, the vendor preferred to finalize the credit at the 
end of the rental term. Installation delays require the temporary generator to stay in place much longer than expected. 
Even though the permanent generator is now installed, manufacturers’ representatives must be scheduled to test the 
specialized equipment before it can go into service. This created a further delay. This requires issuing Contract Change 
Order No. 8 to further extend the use of the temporary generator through end of April 2025. As a result, a total increase of 
$66,944.28 to the temporary generator agreement with Herc is required for February, March and to have the temporary 
generator available through the end of April 2025, when the start-up testing of the new permanent generator is expected 
to be complete. 
Based on the above, staff recommends approval of Contract Change Order No. 8 to increase the value of the agreement by 
$66,944.28, for a revised total agreement amount of $781,731.99, and to extend the Agreement term not to exceed April 
30, 2025. Staff also recommends adding $22,350 to the contingency reserve in case of any unforeseen delays associated 
with start-up testing and putting the new permanent generator into operation. The final testing and startup could be 
delayed due to manufacturers’ schedules. 
To potentially reduce the payments below the requested increase amounts, staff are coordinating with the contractor to 
identify potential opportunities to commission the permanent generator and demobilize the temporary generator as soon 
as possible. In addition, staff are continuing to negotiate potential credits with Herc. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
Sufficient funds are available in the Basins 2 and 3 Collection System Improvements Project (46s003) to fund this contract 
change order and the additional contingency.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
The work addressed by this administrative report is being undertaken to support the Clean Water Program. This project is 
subject to the requirements of the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA), the general components of which are 
included as part of the Final Programmatic Environmental Impact Report (Final PEIR) (SCH No. 201532006) that was 
prepared for the Clean Water Program. The Final PEIR was certified by City Council on June 6, 2016.

Standard Terms and Conditions
Shift Rates:
·        Diesel Engine Powered equipment is priced as Single Shift unless otherwise noted.
1 st Shift - 0-8 hours per day/ up to 40 hrs. per week/ up to 160 hrs. per month
2 nd  Shift - 9-16 hours per day/ 41-80 hrs. per week/ 161-320 hrs. per month – rate x 1.5
3 rd Shift (unlimited hours per day/ week/ month)- rate x 2
Maintenance:
·       By renting this equipment, renter agrees to pay the maintenance surcharge for every hour the unit is run. 
         It is assumed the diesel engine powered equipment is being run 160 hours per month during the rental period. 
           The final invoice will be adjusted to reflect the actual hours used. 
Fuel:
·       Diesel Engine Driven Pumps will be delivered with Fuel Tanks full and should be returned full. 
·       Generators 480kw and above will be delivered with fuel tanks 25% full.  These tanks must be returned with no 
                           more fuel then delivered due to possible weight restrictions and DOT laws.
·        Additional Fuel Cubes with 110% liquid containment are available to supplement the standard 24 hours runtime 
           capacity on each unit.
·       Onsite fuel deliveries can be arranged through Herc Rentals for an additional fee.
·       Refueling at Herc Rentals upon return will be invoiced at published rate.
Labor:
·       Labor for set-up and tear down not included.
·       Requested labor for set-up and tear down can be provided for an additional fee.  Electrical connections to 
          equipment other than owned by Herc are to be outsourced by the customer.
          Labor during business hours- $150./hr.; afterhours $225./hr.; Holidays $500./hr.
·       Onsite per diem if required will be invoiced as additional $200. per night per employee.
·       Final electrical connection by a licensed electrician unless otherwise specified above.
Freight:
·       In house freight services will be billed at $135. per hour during normal business hours plus any wait time. 
·       Outside freight services will be billed on a  cost plus bases during normal business hours plus any wait time. 
·       Offloading and loading upon return by others.  Equipment dimensions and weight rating available if requested.
Terms:
·       Quotations valid for 30 days
·       Equipment availability is subject to prior rental or sale unless PO is accepted prior to delivery.
·       Taxes, fuel fees, environmental fees, delivery are estimates 
·       All permits, license fees, and compliance with city and state codes are the responsibility of the customer.
·       There is an Emissions and Environmental Surcharge of 1.98% applied to the rental charge of motorized
equipment on each invoice. The Emissions and Environmental Surcharge is to help offset the costs of the new
industry emissions standards and environmental laws and regulations at the federal, state and local government
level. This surcharge includes environmental costs and expenses previously charged as part of the Environmental
Recovery Fee.
Insurance and Pro Rental Protection Plan (ProRPP) 
·       The customer is responsible for insuring the equipment and all accessories for full replacement value while in 
         customer’s possession.  The Certificate of Insurance (COI) naming Herc Rentals as additional insured must be on file at least 3 
         business days prior to delivery.
·       Herc Rental  offers a Pro Rental Protection Plan (ProRPP) for an additional fee of 15% of rental charges. 
ProRPP will waive 100 percent of repair /replacement cost or damaged or stolen gear.
When you return damaged or provide a police report for stolen gear, Herc Rentals will cover the
damage or replacement cost. Some exclusion apply contact your local Herc Rentals office for details or see link

Shift Rates:
·
Diesel Engine Powered equipment is priced as Single Shift unless otherwise noted.
1 st Shift - 0-8 hours per day/ up to 40 hrs. per week/ up to 160 hrs. per month
2 nd  Shift - 9-16 hours per day/ 41-80 hrs. per week/ 161-320 hrs. per month – rate x 1.5
3 rd Shift (unlimited hours per day/ week/ month)- rate x 2
Maintenance:
·
By renting this equipment, renter agrees to pay the maintenance surcharge for every hour the unit is run.
It is assumed the diesel engine powered equipment is being run 160 hours per month during the rental period.
 The final invoice will be adjusted to reflect the actual hours used. 
Fuel:
·
Diesel Engine Driven Pumps will be delivered with Fuel Tanks full and should be returned full.
·
Generators 480kw and above will be delivered with fuel tanks 25% full.  These tanks must be returned with no
more fuel then delivered due to possible weight restrictions and DOT laws.
·
Additional Fuel Cubes with 110% liquid containment are available to supplement the standard 24 hours runtime
capacity on each unit.
·
Onsite fuel deliveries can be arranged through Herc Rentals for an additional fee.
·
Refueling at Herc Rentals upon return will be invoiced at published rate.
Labor:
·
Labor for set-up and tear down not included.
·
Requested labor for set-up and tear down can be provided for an additional fee.  Electrical connections to
equipment other than owned by Herc are to be outsourced by the customer.
 Labor during business hours- $150./hr.; afterhours $225./hr.; Holidays $500./hr.
·
Onsite per diem if required will be invoiced as additional $200. per night per employee.
·

Freight:
·

·
Outside freight services will be billed on a  cost plus bases during normal business hours plus any wait time.
·
Offloading and loading upon return by others.  Equipment dimensions and weight rating available if requested.

·
Quotations valid for 30 days
·

All permits, license fees, and compliance with city and state codes are the responsibility of the customer.

industry emissions standards and environmental laws and regulations at the federal, state and local government

Recovery Fee.

SUBJECT:
Consulting Recruitment Services – Change Order 
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Change Order No. 1 to the agreement with It's Personnel Consulting for the purpose of professional recruitment 
services in the amount of $100,000.00 for a new agreement total of $150,000.00; and authorize the City Manager to 
execute the Change Order in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
The City of San Mateo’s agreement with It’s Personnel Consulting effective October 23, 2024 through June 30, 2025 to 
conduct professional recruitment services to fill critical vacancies has an original Purchase Order (PO) amount of 
$50,000.00. In 2024, with It’s Personnel’s recruitment efforts, the City filled 140 vacant positions. As of the beginning of 
the current fiscal year, It’s Personnel has conducted 24 recruitments while the HR recruitment staff participate in Workday 
implementation. HR is requesting to increase the PO amount with It’s Personnel to conduct professional and timely city-
wide recruitment services by $100,000.00 for a total contract of $150,000.00 through June 30, 2025. HR will begin the RFP 
process prior to June 30, 2025, to obtain the best value when retaining professional recruitment services.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The recruitment services conducted by It’s Personnel Consulting are paid for by the recruiting department and there is 
sufficient funding within the department budgets to cover the additional costs.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This change order is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not 
result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

SUBJECT:
Mobile Parking Revenue Collection Amendment – Approval
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 1 to the agreement with PayByPhone US, Inc. for mobile parking payment services in the 
amount of $65,000 for a new agreement total of $150,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the 
amendment in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
The PayByPhone system was first implemented in 2016 and allows patrons the ability to pay for public parking via their 
smartphone. Due to turnover, staff inadvertently allowed the prior agreement with PayByPhone to expire at the end of 
July 2024. In March 2025, to continue mobile payment services and expedite payment for services since expiration of the 
agreement, the City executed a new two-year agreement with PayByPhone US, Inc. (PayByPhone) in the amount of 
$85,000.
The agreement was intended to pay for outstanding PayByPhone invoices from August to November 2024 as well as 
unforeseen miscellaneous fees (i.e., new location numbers, sign fabrication). However, due to a lengthy negotiation 
process, the City incurred additional outstanding invoices from December 2024 through March 2025. There are insufficient 
funds in the existing agreement to pay for the outstanding invoices from December 2024 to March 2025.
City staff recommends increasing the agreement amount by $65,000 for a new total agreement amount of $150,000. The 
added funds will be used to pay the outstanding invoices from December 2024 to March 2025 and unforeseen 
miscellaneous fees. The new agreement includes a revised process under which PayByPhone receives all parking revenue 
remitted via mobile payments. PayByPhone then remits to the City the balance of parking revenue minus PayByPhone's 
costs, thereby eliminating the monthly process of invoicing the City for payment of fees. As such, the proposed 
amendment provides sufficient funding to cover all outstanding invoices and fees, and additional funding is not required 
for the remainder of the agreement timeframe. Staff recommends Council approve proposed Amendment No. 1.  
BUDGET IMPACT:
There are sufficient funds from the Transportation operating budget to fund this amendment.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This City Council action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that there is no possibility 
that approval of an amendment to the Agreement with PaybyPhone to provide mobile parking payment services may have 
a significant effect on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3).)

SUBJECT:
San Mateo Public Library Foundation Operating Lease – Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an Amendment to the Property Lease and Operating Agreement with the San Mateo Public Library Foundation to 
extend the lease for an additional year commencing retroactively on April 1, 2025, through March 31, 2026; and authorize 
its execution by the City Librarian.
BACKGROUND:
The San Mateo Public Library Foundation (SMPLF) leases office space in the Main Library to accommodate Foundation 
employees who perform fund development duties in support of the Library Foundation's mission. The Commercial 
Property Lease Agreement and Operating Agreement between the City of San Mateo and San Mateo Public Library 
Foundation was signed on December 14, 2007. Subsequent lease extensions through March 31, 2025, have been approved 
by the City Council. This Amendment represents a one-year extension of the lease agreement retroactive on April 1, 
through March 31, 2026. 
In FY 2024-25, the Library Foundation awarded $130,000 for support of programs and collections. The successful 2024 and 
2025 fundraising events made it possible for the Library's cultural committees to provide cultural and educational events 
to the public as well as enhance the Library's general collection.
BUDGET IMPACT:
In consideration of the financial support the SMPF fulfills on behalf of the San Mateo Public Library, the rental amount of 
the lease will continue to be set at the nominal rate of $12 per annum.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This lease is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is a government fiscal activity which does not involve any 
commitment to any specific project which may result in a potentially significant physical impact on the environment. 
(CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

SUBJECT:
SEIU Local 521, Maintenance, Side Letter of Agreement Regarding Salary Increase - Adoption
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to amend the SEIU Local 521, Maintenance Memorandum of Understanding to implement additional 
equity salary adjustments.
BACKGROUND:
During contract negotiations with SEIU Local 521, Maintenance (“SEIU”), an agreement was made to meet and confer 
regarding the findings of a total compensation survey and potential additional equity adjustments for the following 
classifications: 1. Custodian, 2. Tree Maintenance Specialist and 3. Traffic and Lighting Technician. 
In the fall of 2024, SEIU exercised its right under Section 31.3 to request a classification and compensation review of the 
following three classifications 1. Maintenance Planner, 2. Instrument Control Technician and 3. Wastewater Treatment 
Plant Electrical Technician based on sustained recruitment or retention difficulties.
Based on the findings of the total compensation surveys, the City and SEIU agreed via a Side letter of Agreement to the 
following equity salary increase effective the first full pay period following Council adoption: 
•
Traffic and Lighting Technician- 0.25 percent,
•
Custodian- 2.46 percent, 
•
Maintenance Planner- 11.16 percent,
•
Instrument Control Technician- 11.16 percent,
•
Wastewater Treatment Plant Electrical Technician- 11.16 percent 
BUDGET IMPACT:
The additional compensation will result in an annual increase of approximately $112,000, with $4,200 in the General Fund, 
$101,400 in the Sewer Fund, and $6,400 in the Fleet and Facilities Fund.
